MOHAMMAD WASIM                                     Petitioner(s)

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Heard Mr. Abhisar Bhanu, learned counsel for the
petitioner,  Ms.  Sansriti  Pathak,  learned  Additional
1

--- Page 8 ---
Advocate General, appearing for the State and Mr. Amit
Pai, learned Amicus Curiae, appearing for the de-facto
complainant.
2. This petitioner calls in question the correctness
of  the  order  dated  16.02.2026  in  S.B.  Criminal
Miscellaneous Bail Application No. 16120/2025, passed by
the High Court of Judicature at Rajasthan at Jaipur. By
the said said order, the petitioner has been denied the
benefit of bail in connection with FIR No.345/2025,
registered at Police Station – Jaisinghpura Khor, Jaipur
North, for the offences punishable under Sections 64(1)
of the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023 (for short, ‘BNS’)
and 3 and 4 of the Protection of Children from Sexual
Offences Act, 2012 (for short, ‘POCSO’). 
3. Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that
the petitioner had already undergone eight months in
custody. Learned counsel also draws attention to the
deposition  of  PW-1  (prosecutrix)  and  submits  that
admittedly, the prosecutrix refused to undergo medical
examination. He also draws attention to that portion of
the statement, where the prosecutrix admitted that the
room, in which the incident is alleged to have happened,
was taken by her, and not provided by the accused.
Learned counsel for the petitioner also submits that
earlier, there was a similar case instituted against
2

--- Page 9 ---
one,  Jamir  Afridi,  which  resulted  in  an  acquittal
because the prosecutrix recanted from her statement. He
further submits that the trial is bound to take some
time, since five witnesses remained to be examined.
4. Learned counsel for the State and learned Amicus
Curiae, defend the impugned order.
5. Having  considered  the  overall  facts  and
circumstances of the case and considering the period
undergone, we are inclined to enlarge the petitioner on
bail.
6. Accordingly, we direct that the petitioner be
enlarged on bail subject to the satisfaction of the
Trial  Court,  in  connection  with  Sessions  Case  No.
02/2025,  pending  on  the  court  of  Special  Judge
Protection of Children from Sexual Offences Act 2012,
Serial No. 01, Jaipur Metropolitan, II.
7. We place on record our appreciation to Mr. Amit
Pai,  learned  Amicus  Curiae  who  ably  prepared  and
presented the case. 
8. The Special Leave Petition is disposed of in the
above terms.
9. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand
disposed of.

ITEM NO.1               COURT NO.3               SECTION II-C
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition(s) for Special Leave to Appeal (Crl.) No(s). 11604/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  05-01-2026
in MCRC No. 10498/2025 passed by the High Court of Chhatisgarh at
Bilaspur]
DEEPAK SINGH                                       Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
STATE OF CHHHATTISGARH                             Respondent(s)
IA No. 178235/2026 - CONDONATION OF DELAY IN FILING
IA No. 178233/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT
IA No. 178232/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 02-07-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE K.V. VISWANATHAN
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE SHREE CHANDRASHEKHAR
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Raj Kumar, Adv.
                   Mr. Ajay Singh, Adv.
                   Mr. Vipin Nagar, Adv.
                   Ms. Chanchal Sharma, Adv.
                   Mr. Jugul Kishor Gupta, AOR
                   Mr. Kamal Chaudhary, Adv.
                   Mr. Vasim Akhter, Adv.
                   
                   
For Respondent(s) :Mr. Piyush, Standing counsel 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Heard  Mr.  Raj  Kumar,  learned  counsel  for  the
petitioner and Mr. Piyush, learned standing counsel for the
1

--- Page 22 ---
State.
2. The petitioner calls in question the correctness of
the order  dated 05.01.2026 in MCRC No. 10498 of 2025,
passed by the High Court of Judicature at Chhattisgarh at
Bilaspur. By the said order, the petitioner has been denied
the benefit of bail in connection with FIR No.1/2025,
registered with Tongpal Police Station, District Sukma,
Chhattisgarh,  for the offences punishable under Sections
20(b)(ii)(C)  of  the  Narcotic  Drugs  and  Psychotropic
Substances Act, 1985 (for short, ‘NDPS Act’).
3. Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that the
petitioner has been in custody for 01 year and 05 months.
Learned  counsel  also  submits  that  the  petitioner  is
entitled to bail on the ground of parity. In this regard,
learned counsel draws attention to the order of this court
in SLP (Crl.) No. 5879 of 2026, titled as “Rinku Prasad vs.
State of Chhattisgarh” . Learned counsel submits that the
prosecution  story  is  that  the  contraband  was  jointly
recovered from the possession of petitioner and the co-
accused Rinku Prasad. Learned counsel also submits that the
co-accused Rinku Prasad has had the benefit of bail and the
petitioner also be enlarged on bail.
4. Learned counsel for the State, however, vehemently
defend the impugned order.
2

--- Page 23 ---
5. We have carefully considered the submissions of the
learned counsel and kept in mind the principles mentioned
in Section 37 of the NDPS Act. We have also perused the
bail order of co-accused Rinku Prasad. The petitioner is
entitled to parity with co-accused Rinku Prasad. Petitioner
has also undergone custody of 01 year and 05 months and the
trial is bound to take some time for conclusion. Having
considered the overall facts and circumstances of the case,
we are inclined to enlarge the petitioner on bail.
6. Accordingly,  we  direct  that  the  petitioner  be
enlarged on bail subject to the satisfaction of the Special
Judge  (NDPS  Act),  Dantewada,  District  South  Bastar
Dantewada  (70G),  Chhattisgarh,  in  connection  with  the
aforesaid FIR for the offences mentioned hereinabove.
7. The Special Leave Petition is disposed of in the
above terms.
8. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand
disposed of.
  (RAHUL KUMAR)                                 (MANOJ KUMAR)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)
3

--- Page 24 ---

for the petitioner and Mr. Rajan K.Chourasia , learned

--- Page 31 ---
2
counsel for the State. 
3. The present Special Leave Petition calls in question
the correctness of the order dated 23-03-2026 in MCRLC
No. 9484/2026 passed by the High Court of Madhya
Pradesh at Indore. By the said order, the petitioner
has been declined the benefit of bail in connection
with  FIR/Crime  No.809/2023  registered  with  Police
Station  Banganga,  District  Indore  Urban,  Madhya
Pradesh,  for the offences punishable under Sections
408, 420, 467, 468 and 471 of the Indian Penal Code,
1860.
4. Learned Senior Counsel for the petitioner submits
that the petitioner is in custody since 03.02.2026 and
the petitioner already undergone about 05 months in
custody. The offences are Magistrate triable. Learned
Senior Counsel for the petitioner submits that grave
prejudice  is  caused,  if  he  continued  to  be
incarcerated.
5. Learned counsel for the State vehemently opposes the
bail application.
6. Considering the overall facts and circumstances of
the case and considering the period undergone by the
petitioner as also the nature of the offences, we are
inclined to enlarge the petitioner on bail.
7. Accordingly,  we  direct  that  the  petitioner  be
enlarged on bail su bject to the satisfaction of the
concerned Trial Court in connection with the aforesaid

--- Page 32 ---
3
FIR/Crime for the offences mentioned hereinabove.
8. The Special Leave Petition is disposed of in the
above terms.
9. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand
disposed of.

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following

1. Having  heard  Mr.  Parveen  Kumar,  learned  AOR  for  the
1

--- Page 53 ---
petitioner(s) and Mr. Jayesh Gaurav, learned counsel appearing
after notice for the respondent, we are not inclined to interfere
with the impugned order. Hence, the Special Leave Petition stands
dismissed. However, we make it clear that the trial will be held
uninfluenced by any of the observations made in the order of the
High Court.
2. Learned counsel for the petitioners pray for dispensing with
their personal presence at the trial. It is needless to state that
there are remedies provided for in the Code and as and when the

                             O R D E R
Delay condoned.
We do not find any merit in this petition.
Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that
the High Court has granted six months’ time to the
petitioner to vacate the premises, which is going to
expire in September, 2026. He prays that the petitioner
may be granted further three more months to do so.
1

--- Page 75 ---
In view of the above submission, we dismiss
this petition by granting further three months time,
beyond the six months time granted to the petitioner
by the High Court, to vacate the premises , subject to
the petitioner furnishing usual undertaking before
this Court within two weeks from today, stating that
the petitioner will not create any third party rights,
clear all the arrears and continue to pay the rent
regularly in the meanwhile and will also peacefully
vacate the premises concerned on or before the expiry
of the aforesaid period.
Pending application(s) shall stand disposed of.

(the petitioner herein) contending, inter-alia, that in
view of the fact that the financial assistance received
from the State of Haryana, on account of the death of
his son, is being enjoyed primarily by the wife of his

1

--- Page 113 ---
and the petitioner is not able to enjoy the benefits of
the financial assistance and with the deduction of the

receive a meagre amount as his share.

No.2 will be necessary for the just determination of
the case.
3. In view of the above, the petitioner may take
fresh steps for service of notice on Respondent No.2 to
ensure her presence before this Court.
4. In addition, service through Dasti mode is also
permitted.
